## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical concentration A, which is typically modeled by kinetic rate laws dA_dt = f(A, t) describing reaction order, reversibility (approach to equilibrium), autocatalysis, inhibition/saturation, or time-varying rate constants due to changing conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., catalyst/photolysis limited by external flux)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay or pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or 2A -> products)
- n-th order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order, possibly non-integer)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (reversible reaction reduced to relaxation toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / limited-growth form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (A promotes its own production but is limited by depletion/capacity c1)
- General polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (mixture of zero/first/second-order contributions, side reactions)
- Inhibition/saturation of decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (effective rate decreases at high A due to inhibition/limited active sites)
- Time-varying first-order (linear drift in k): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes approximately linearly in time)
- Time-varying first-order (exponential ramp in k): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate accelerates/decelerates exponentially with time-dependent conditions)
- Driven production plus decay: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (constant source term with first-order loss; open system or inflow/outflow approximation)
- Stretched-exponential–like kinetics (in derivative form): dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (dispersive kinetics / time-dependent effective rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A (straight line through origin in dA_dt vs A), it indicates first-order kinetics with constant k.
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over a wide range of A, it suggests zero-order control (rate limited by external supply/flux or surface saturation).
- Curvature consistent with dA_dt scaling like A**2 (or higher powers) indicates higher-order elementary steps or effective kinetics from multiple species lumped into A.
- A zero crossing near A = c1 with opposite signs on either side suggests approach to equilibrium (reversibility) modeled by (A - c1).
- A factor A*(c1 - A) implies autocatalysis with depletion/finite capacity; the rate vanishes at A = 0 and A = c1 and peaks at intermediate A.
- Rational forms like A/(1 + c*A) indicate inhibition or saturation of reactive sites, giving sub-linear growth of |dA_dt| at high A.
- Explicit dependence on t in the coefficient multiplying A indicates a time-varying rate constant (changing temperature, light intensity, catalyst deactivation).
- A constant source term c0 combined with a loss term -c1*A implies an open/reactor-like balance with a steady-state concentration A ≈ c0/(c1).
- Non-integer powers of A or t often reflect heterogeneous/dispersive kinetics (e.g., diffusion limitations, fractal-like reaction environments).

GT: -c0*A**c1 - c2*A + c3*_t*sin(log(A + c4))
Candidates evaluated: 59
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.6789593965981179*A**2 - 0.6789593965981179*A + 0.1640697849676163*sin(log(A + 1))`

The GT has three terms:
1. A quadratic term: `-0.6790*A²`
2. A linear term: `-0.6790*A`
3. A sin(log(A+1)) term: `0.1641*sin(log(A+1))`

Note: `_t` is a constant (0.2416...), so `c3*_t` = 0.6790 * 0.2416 ≈ 0.1641.

The GT is a function of A only (t appears only as a fixed constant `_t`). So any candidate with explicit `t` dependence must have those `t`-dependent terms either reducible to constants or zeroed out.

Let me analyze each candidate:

**Candidate 1:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c2*t + c3*|A|^c4 + c5 + c6*exp(c7*cos(c8*log(c9*|A|+1)))`
Has explicit `t` dependence via `c2*t`. Set c2=0. Then: `A²*c0 + A*c1 + c3*|A|^c4 + c5 + c6*exp(c7*cos(c8*log(c9*|A|+1)))`. With A≥0, |A|=A. Set c3=0 (or c4 to merge with existing terms). We need `sin(log(A+1))` but have `exp(c7*cos(c8*log(c9*A+1)))`. The exponential of cosine cannot equal sin. **NO MATCH.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2+1) + c3 + c4*log(c5*exp(A*c6+c7*t)+1)`
The `log(exp(...)+1)` is a softplus-like function, not sin(log(...)). Cannot match.

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2+1) + A*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*sin(A*c6+c7) + c8`
Set c4=0 to make exp(c4*t)=1. Then: `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2+1) + A*c3 + c5*sin(A*c6+c7) + c8`. 
First part: `A*(c0+c3) + A*c1/(A*c2+1) + c8`. With common denominator: `[A*(c0+c3)*(A*c2+1) + A*c1 + c8*(A*c2+1)]/(A*c2+1)`.
This gives a rational function in A plus `sin(A*c6+c7)`. GT has `sin(log(A+1))`, not `sin(linear in A)`. These are fundamentally different functions.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A*c2+1) + A^c3*c4/(A^c3+c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8) + c9`
